Annex 11
SRI LANKA
TEACHER EDUCATION AND DEPLOYMENT PROJECT
DETAILED PROJECT DESCRIPTION
Component A: Rationalization of Teacher Deployment (estimated baseline cost US$0.2
million):
1.     Teacher recruitment and deployment practices and mechanisms would be modified to improve
response to demand while increasing equity and reducing teacher costs. This policy based activity would
reactivate the use of existing and updated teacher allocation mechanisms, and formalize the efforts
underway since 1995 to standardize the teacher cadre and link it to budgetary allocations. The revised
formula takes into consideration actual teacher needs based on student enrollments, the existing teacher
cadre, and the annual attrition of teachers from the system (loss due to retirement, death, departure etc.),
in allocation of teachers at the primary and secondary levels in all the provinces. The application of the
formula and associated mechanisms would allocate a specific cadre of teachers to each province and
school and, in turn, trigger annual agreed and fixed budgetary allocations to be determined by a new
Cadre Committee (see below) and used by MOF in making payments to the provinces. The agreed
program provides that within a period of three years the number of teachers should be rationalized.
2.     The objective of this component would be to improve the quality, equity and cost-effectiveness of
the staffing of schools through: (i) controlling teacher recruitment below attrition and apply the modified
Ready Reckoner to achieve STR targets of 26:1 for primary and 22:1 for secondary by year 2001 (see
Annex 3 for details on the application of the RR); (ii) applying the RR consistently to all schools (with
stringent provisions for variations to cater for exceptional circumstances); (iii) relating teacher demand
projection analysis to teacher supply with annual adjustments; (iv) linking the cadre entitlement for each
province to the budget allocation for salaries; (v) utilizing salary savings for quality inputs, particularly
in disadvantaged areas; (vi) requiring all teachers entering the service to have successfully completed an
accredited teacher education program (with strict criteria being applied to the appointment of untrained
teachers, where required, to meet staffing emergencies in specific situations).
3.     To achieve the above objectives, the project would strengthen the capacity of MEHE to: (i)
collect and analyze data on teacher needs, and carry out demand projections; (ii) develop strategies for
linking these needs to national supply capacity; and (iii) regulate the annual teacher trainee intake and
deployment of trained teachers. The driving mechanisms would be the annual application of modified RR
formula for staff deployment, together with linked budgetary allocations. The salary savings resulting
from the stricter application of the RR would be reallocated to quality inputs and maintenance. The goal
would be to increase the present national average allocation of 3 percent for quality inputs (but as low as I
percent in some provinces) by about 1 percent per year reaching a minimum of 6 percent by the end of the
project.
4.     MERE, in consultation with Provincial Education Authorities, would be responsible for the
annual collection and analysis of teacher demand information and for the preparation of an annual report
on short and long-term staffing needs. Provincial authorities would only be allocated teacher salary
resources when their annual retrospective staffing and following year staffing plan (cadre) were submitted
and agreement on allocation reached.
5.     The approved cadre would be determined annually by a Teacher Cadre Committee (TCC)
consisting of representatives of MEHE (including the Chairman of the MEHE Teacher Transfers Board),
NATE, Ministry of Finance (MOF) which would coordinate the committee, Finance Commission and two
Provincial Representatives (nominated by Provincial Directors of Education), in consultation with
83



Education Service Comnmittee (ESC). The functions and structure of the proposed TCC are outlined in
Annex 14.
6.     The recurrent teacher salary expenditure allocation for each Province as determined by the TCC
would include a margin of 2 percent of approved salary expenditure to cover special circumstances. This
margin would commence at a higher rate for those provinces which are under-staffed. For provinces
which have more staff than the accepted cadre, a staff equalization plan should be agreed to by MEHE,
ESC, MOF and each relevant province.
7.     Provinces which were over-staffed and did not meet the agreed staff equalization plan would not
be allowed to augment salary expenditures from other sources and would have to consider the student unit
cost allocations for various inputs (being developed by MEHE). Provinces which were understaffed and
were unable to attract staff under the agreed staff equalization plan would, following the development of a
suitable support and incentive plan for targeted schools, be allocated additional funds. As part of the
teacher monitoring provisions, the provinces would, in consultation with the ESC, develop during the first
year of the project measures to track teacher absenteeism. Teachers who continued to take non-approved
or excessive absenteeism (beyond dates mandated) would have their remuneration reviewed. Provinces
could then utilize unpaid funds to pay the costs of substitute teachers while being aware that no
supplementary salary allocations would be made for teachers with excessive absenteeism.
8.     The newly-appointed Transfer Boards created at zonal, provincial and ministry levels under the
1995 National Policy on Teachers Transfers, would have a critical role to play in the redistribution of staff
to achieve greater equity (Annex 5). Strict application of the requirements for initial appointment to
"non-congenial" (for a minimum of 4 years) and to "difficult" schools (for a minimum of 3 years) and for
transfer of teachers after serving a maximum of 8 years in a "congenial" and 6 years in a "very congenial"
school, would be essential. Provision would also be made through the initial and continuing education
programs for teachers to broaden areas of teaching competence. Secondary teachers should be able to
teach a minimum of one major and at least one minor subject, thereby increasing staffing flexibility and
MEHE's ability to allocate secondary and collegiate teachers more equitably.
9.     MEBE (through the Policy, Planning and Review Division) in consultation with ESC would be
responsible for designing a comprehensive plan to attract teachers to, and support teachers in schools in
less favorable and/or remote areas. The plan would be based on the newly-formulated categorization of
schools into four groups, according to degrees of hardship. This plan would be funded from the savings
on teacher salaries (as a result of applying the revised RR) and provide: (i) differential allowances based
on the degree of hardships; (ii) differential location allowances on an escalating basis corresponding to the
years of service in a particular location; (iii) consideration of years of service in less favorable schools to
be used as one of the main criteria for transfer to more favorable schools; (iv) support for teacher travel
and housing (local standards); (v) special provision to facilitate teacher access to study opportunities,
including payment of partial to full fees and assistance with travel to study centers; and (vi) support for
the education of the teacher's children where there is no secondary school available locally.
10.    As a further measure to facilitate equitable and flexible deployment, particularly on initial
appointment to hardship areas ("non-congenial" and "difficult" schools). Recent increases in salaries for
teachers should assist. Other initiatives which should be considered by MEHE and the proposed National
Authority on Teacher Education (NATE) include: (i) changing the policy on residential requirement for
initial training in undergraduate programs; (ii) increasing the number of non-residential training places;
(Mii) increasing stipends for married trainees; (iv) offering housing assistance on first appointment in
designated hardship areas for married teachers; and (v) assisting with the secondary education costs of the
children of teachers willing to remain in rural areas. For the above activities, the project would support
57 person months of technical assistance outlined in Annex 15. Terms of reference for each consultant
have been prepared and are included in the Implementation Volume.
84



Component B: Rationalization of Structure and Oreanization (estimated baseline cost US$
0.9million).
11.    The objective of this component would be to establish a national framework for an integrated and
cost-effective system of teacher education, with coordinating organizations covering all institutions
involved in training teachers. The component would strengthen the existing unit of the Teacher
Education Commissioner within the MEHE, and establish a new National Authority to develop policy and
to coordinate training institutions. It would support restructuring of the system to consist of: (i) a newly-
established National Authority on Teacher Education (NATE) for overall policy development, planning,
coordination, standardization (including accreditation of programs) and monitoring of teacher education;
(ii) three types of training institutions offering initial and continuing teacher education by direct and
distance mode - Universities, NEE and National Colleges of Education (NCOEs); and (iii) Teachers
Centers (TCs) Type A and Type B (TEIs) which would serve as a resource base for teachers in local areas,
a learning and administrative outlet for distance education activities, and a center for the delivery of
continuing education courses. Where appropriate, TCs Type A and Type B (TEIs) could also provide a
base for advisors working with teachers in local schools and/or for English language courses for teachers
in the area.
12.    The proposed restructuring would: (i) provide the framework for coordinating all aspects of
teacher education on a national basis, including the essential linking of teacher demand with supply
through the training institutions; (ii) provide sufficient initial training places to meet the national need
for trained teachers; (iii) concentrate initial teacher education in larger and more economical institutions,
centrally located in the mnain population centers, thereby increasing the proportion of students in non-
residential places; (iv) progressively transform distance mode teacher training from initial certificate to
diploma, graduate diploma courses, and to continuing education; (v) achieve a better coverage of staff
expertise in areas of specialization within each institution; and (vi) establish and safeguard standards for
teacher education programs through a national accreditation and monitoring mechanism.
13.    During appraisal agreement was reached to restructure the management of teacher education and
to establish NATE. NATE would be a semi-autonomous body responsible to the Minister for Education
and Higher Education, within the structure of MEHE, and funded as a separate entity. The principal
function of NATE would be to advise the MEHE on major issues relating to teacher education on a
national basis. This will involve: (i) developing national policy on, and planning for, teacher education,
facilitating the implementation of the integrated national system; (ii) monitoring and research; and (iii)
provision of public information on teacher education. The governing body would comprise
representatives from: the three types of teacher education institutions - Universities, NIE and NCOEs; the
Chief Commissioner for Teacher Education; Provincial Education Authorities; NEC; Ministry of National
Planning; Ministry of Finance; Education Service Board; and schools. NATE would have a part-time
chairman, a full-time director and secretariat (4 professionals and 5 administrative officers, with provision
for secondment of specialized personnel). The project would support the recurrent budget for NATE on a
declining basis. Further details on structure, relationships, functions, membership, staffing and funding
support for NATE are provided in Annex 17.
14.    NATE would have a key role in regulating the supply of trained teachers to meet projected
demand in schools as finalized through the Cadre Committee on school staffing entitlements. NATE
would make recomnmendations to the Minister, MEHE, annually, on the intake of students by discipline
for each teacher education institution. It would also advise the Minister, MEHE, on the budget
requirements for each teacher education institution, based on student enrollments and unit costs for
different types of progranms. All teacher education programs would be subject to accreditation through
NATE. This would involve peer review of programs through a NATE Accreditation Standing Comnmittee.
Further, NATE, in consultation with the teacher education institutions, would be responsible for
establishing and overview of criteria for the selection, appointment, training and promotion for teacher
educators. Two initial responsibilities of NATE would be (i) to assess the equivalency of the current COE
85



Diploma in Teaching with the Certificates in Teaching awarded by the TTCs and NIE Distance
Education, and (ii) to start the process of training needs assessment. NATE would be responsible for
coordinating the design and development of a comprehensive continuing education plan and for the
accreditation of courses deemed appropriate for recognition towards a further qualification. These
activities would require technical assistance.
15.    During appraisal Government endorsed: (i) the rationalization of Colleges of Education and
Teacher Training Colleges into National Colleges of Education (NCOEs) and TCs both Type A and Type
B (TEIs); (ii) the development of some 81 Teacher Centers distributed strategically across all provinces;
and (iii) the inclusion of N1E and the faculties/departments of education of the four universities that train
teachers (Colombo, Peradeniya, Jaffna and Open University) into the integrated national system. The
proposed structure of the reformed teacher education system is outlined in Annex 16. The Office of the
Chief Commissioner for Teacher Education would be given a clearer mandate within MEHE and be
strengthened through provision of additional staff and equipment.
16.    NCOEs would be national institutions, within MEHE, responsible to the Chief Commissioner for
Teacher Education (see Annex 18). Their principal focus in the short to medium term would be on initial
training to diploma level and on short continuing teacher education courses. These programs would be
developed by the NIE national teacher education curriculum committee whose membership includes
NCOEs, Universities and schools. NCOEs would normally offer 3 to 4 disciplines for an enrollment of
around 700-1,000 students (including 300 third year students in their internship year in schools), with a
physical capacity of 500-800, and provision for residential and non-residential students. In the longer
term, with NATE's agreement, NCOEs could provide both initial and continuing education courses up to
but not including masters level. NCOEs would be given a direct budget allocation, based on NATE's
recommendations, and increased financial autonomy, under delegation through the Chief Commissioner
for Teacher Education. The Chief Commissioner for Teacher Education would continue to be responsible
to the Secretary, MEHE for the overall operation and accountability of NCOEs, in close consultation with
NATE and provincial directors of education. The Chief Commissioner would retain responsibility for
allocating individual students to NCOEs and for staffing NCOEs, under guidelines agreed through NATE
(and in accordance with the provisions of the Teacher Educator Service). For each NCOE there will be an
external Conunittee on Continuing Teacher Education, chaired by the NCOE president or vice-president.
Membership would include the Director, Continuing Teacher Education; principals of the TCs which are
run by that NCOE; the Director, Provincial Education (or nominee); representatives from institutions
operating continuing education courses for teachers through the TCs, and from relevant schools. The
principal functions of the committee would be to advise the Director, Continuing Teacher Education on
the quality and relevance of courses; the allocation of resources; matters relating to teacher access;
requirements for future course offerings, and associated resource needs.
17.    The Teachers Centers (TCs) would be integral parts of the NCOEs. Each NCOE would have
within its organizational structure a number of TCs, assigned according to location and other strategic
factors. NCOEs would receive funding for the full operation of the assigned TCs as a specific item within
their annual budget. Most TCs would employ a full time principal and about three lecturers (trained in
distance teaching), together with administrative support. The full-time TC staff would be part of the staff
of the relevant NCOE. The TC head would be directly responsible to the Director, Continuing Teacher
Education within each NCOE, would work closely with the province/district education officers and with
other training institutions who are offering courses for teachers through that TC. Some 84 Teacher
Centers would be developed (renovated, furnished and equipped), having particular regard to
demographic and access factors. There would be two types of TCs, Type A TCs (84 in number) with
capacity for about 100 teachers at one time, would cater to teachers who can attend on a daily basis (week
days and week-ends). Type A TCs would serve as (i) a center for the delivery of continuing education
courses (ranging from half day to three weeks); (ii) a resource base for teachers in the local area; (iii) a
learning and administrative outlet for distance mode teacher education activities (run by both universities
and NIE); (iv) a base for advisors working with teachers in local schools, where appropriate; and (iv) a
86



center for the delivery of English language teaching for teachers, if required. Type B (TEIs) (3 in
number) would offer residential facilities for continuing education courses for teachers without reasonable
daily access to Type A TCs. They may also offer the same non-residential services as Type A TCs.
Details of the location of the proposed TCs are provided in Annex 19.
18.    The Faculties/Departments of Education at the universities would provide initial teacher
education both in the disciplines to be taught in schools and in educational methodology, through either a
first integrated degree (B.Ed.) or post graduate diploma (Dip.Ed.) programs. In addition, these
institutions would, on a selective basis, continue nationally to develop programs to doctorate level. The
faculties would continue to operate under the academic structures of their institutions. In order to receive
funding for teacher education programs (suggested on a trainee unit cost basis) the selected universities
would have to agree to and participate within, the integrated national system, under policies adopted by
Govermnent on the advice of NATE. In particular, this would involve the allocation of teacher trainee
places consistent with national needs; selection of students based on agreed minimal criteria; agreed
student:teacher ratios; and the accreditation of courses by NATE.
19.    The National Institute for Education (NIE) would continue to develop programs for initial and
continuing teacher education, having a central role in developing courses for delivery by both NIE and
NCOEs. Ii would also deliver continuing education programs to upgrade teachers through the distance
mode, including diplomas in education, B.Ed degrees, and post-graduate diplomas in education and
management. Given the change-over to initial training for all teachers entering the service, NIE's delivery
role should decline over time. It would work closely with the Universities and NATE to ensure the
compatibility of course offerings and, in the case of the Open University, to share expertise on the design
and delivery of courses through the distance mode. NIE would continue to help in the professional
development of teacher educators, particularly those in NCOEs and TCs. Professional courses for teacher
educators, run by NIE, would be designed on the basis of national subject-based needs assessments,
undertaken by NATE, in all NCOEs. (See Staffing and Staff Development, below.). Technical assistance
support for NATE and the Comrmissioner of Teacher Education totaling 46 person months are outlined in
Annex 15.
Component C: UDprading of Teacher Education Programs (estimated baseline cost US$3.7 million)
20.    Both initial and continuing programs would be improved, to create a better learning climate in
the schools by raising the quality of teaching, and to make the teacher education programs more cost-
effective.
21.    The objective of the initial (preservice) teacher education program would be to prepare all
teachers prior to their entry into the teaching service. Successful completion would be a pre-requisite for
all seeking appointment as a teacher. Initial teacher education for secondary teachers would be provided
in universities (Post Graduate Diploma in Education and Bachelor of Education) and in National Colleges
of Education for primary teachers. Initial teacher education of two years would be conducted in NCOEs
followed by a one year internship prior to the award of a Diploma in Teaching. The curriculum is being
revised, with ADB assistance, to contain three major areas: general, professional and specialized
discipline/subject knowledge (Annex 9). Each NCOE has been assigned geographically in response to
enrollments and teacher needs and specific subject requirements by specialization (Annex 20A and 20B).
Student enrollment would be based on the projected demand for subject teachers. Entry to NCOEs would
require a minimum of 3 subject passes at A level. Each student would select one major with one or two
minor subject disciplines. Initial proposals for the subjects and hours allocated to each year of study
would reduce the total number of contact periods from the present 35 to between 28 and 23 per semester.
Teaching observation and practice in affiliated schools would be an essential component during each year
of the program. Within the next ten years, as the country is expected to move towards a degree teacher
87



force, a three year Bachelor of Education (B.Ed.) should be developed for NCOEs and selected
universities, to replace the present two year course in NCOEs.
22.    The objective of the continuing (inservice) teacher education program is to improve the quality
of teachers already in the teaching service. This sub-component builds on and complements the present
distance education program (assisted by SIDA) which has been making important progress in providing a
first level certification to untrained teachers. Of the 48 percent of teachers now untrained, about 30,000
will obtain their first certificate in 1996, another 15,000 in 1997 and 10,000 in 1998 (leaving about 15
percent untrained). The continuing education program, as expanded by the Project, would thus continue
the important work of giving all untrained teachers a first training, and in addition undertake further
upgrading and offer refresher courses for lowly qualified teachers. The content and scope of courses in
continuing teacher education would change based upon the outcomes of on-going needs assessments of
teachers (para 2.24), through course design and syllabi prepared by NIE utilizing technical assistance.
Courses would be offered in all teacher education institutions - Universities, NIE and NCOEs (including
TCs). The strategy would be to offer four major types of continuing teacher education courses: (i)
upgrading; (ii) broadening; (iii) re-training; and (iv) refresher courses. These courses with costs estimated
at US$3.2 million (costed as part of staff development) are outlined in Annex 21.
23.    The project would support the following technical assistance, overseas assignments and
fellowships: (i) 51 consultant months for program design and courses outlines (see Annex 15 for
details); (ii) 42 consultant months for teacher educator training in new programs and 180 persons months
for curriculum development of pre-service teacher education programs; (iii) 40 consultant months for the
design, update and development of continuing programs; (iv) 6 international consultants for assessment
and modification of certification and 10 consultant months of national consultants to conduct pilot needs
assessment; (v) 48 consultant months for national curriculum development at NIE; (vi) three consultant
months to update and develop student selection criteria; (vii) annual seminars for teacher educators; (viii)
fund annually approved pilot initiatives in teacher education; and (ix) update and develop continuing
education materials and their printing costs.
24.    The Project would also support the procurement of books for libraries, equipment and educational
materials at each of the following; (i) at Faculties of Education in the universities of Colombo, Peradeniya
and Jaffna up to US$120,000 and for the Faculty of Education at Open University US$75,000; (ii) at NIE,
US$120,000 for the Department of Distance Education and US$80,000 for the Department of Teacher
Education; (iii) at 78 Type A for books, equipment and educational materials, US$ 10,000; (iv) at 3 Type
B TCs (TEIs) for equipment and educational material US$180,000; (v) at existing NCOEs equipment and
educational material allocations ranging from US$100,000 to 300,000, depending on needs; and (vi) at
new NCOEs about US$ 300,000 for equipment and educational materials for a total of US$2.3 million.
Component D: Strengtheninine of Staff and Manaeement: (estimated baseline cost US$11.2 million -
including continuing education).
25.    The proposed 14 NCOEs and 84 Type A TCs and 3 Type B TCs (TEIs) would require a total of
about 190 administrative and about 1110 academic staff. Staffing numbers for the NCOEs are listed in
Annex 23. Staffing of the four universities and NE (Department of Distance Education and Department
of Teacher Education) central campuses would remain at approximately the current level of about 160.
These numbers indicate almost the same number of teacher educators as in 1994, when there were about
700 academic staff in the 10 COEs and 16 TTCs, 160 academic staff in universities, 250 senior tutors in
NIE study centers and a number of tutors in regional study centers for which there are no official data.
During the first two years of the project conversion would be made to the new staffing structure. The
majority of staff appointments would be made from the existing staff at COEs, TTCs and study centers
and would be based on agreed criteria outlined in Annex 24. Staff in NCOEs, including TCs, would
88



belong to the Teacher Educator cadre. Part-time staff may be required for specific courses and could be
recruited locally as needed.
26.    A data base of existing teacher educators has been compiled and analyzed to determine their
training needs in the context of institutional responsibilities. The project would provide opportunities for
staff who meet agreed criteria to improve their teacher education qualifications and experience. Staff with
only a first degree or less are the main candidates for staff development (Annex 23 outlines the teacher
educator staff development proposals). The goal would be to maintain following 1999, a more highly
qualified Teacher Educator Service comprising about 10 percent with PhDs, 45 percent with Masters
degrees, 35-40 percent with advanced diplomas, and about 10-15 percent with a first degree
27.    The staff development plan, financed under the project, would cover the following:
(a) Long-term fellowships: about 250 long-term fellowships (about 25 percent of proposed staff
in universities, NCOEs, TCs and NIE) would be awarded: of which about 150 educators would
further their studies within Sri Lanka ($675,000); 50 would attend training in regional countries
($400,000); and another 50 would study in OECD countries ($3.0 million). Training would cover
both content knowledge and specific courses in pedagogy. Costs are based on two years of study
for each teacher educator, usually at post-graduate level.
(b) Linkages with overseas institutions: About four teacher education institutions would be
identified overseas as link institutions. They would be the focal point for work assignments,
exchanges and training of staff. Selected national teacher educators (20 educators for 3 month
internships each year over a period of 4 years for a total of $600,000) would work alongside
overseas colleagues at link institutions to learn modern techniques and approaches to teacher
education. At the same time, teacher educators from the link institutions would visit Sri Lanka
(6 staff for about 2 months per year for 4 years for a total cost of about $720,000) to conduct
courses and seminars. The costs of establishing and maintaining these linkages are estimated at
$10,000 per institution. To support the effective and continuous exchange of knowledge and
experiences with the link institutions and avail the teacher training institutions of the "ERIC
education library service" the project would also support a computer network (Internet). The
unit cost of the equipment needed for 19 local institutions (14 NCOEs, 4 Faculties of Education,
NIE) and MEHE/NATE (total of 20) is estimated at S 100,000. Internet time use is estimated at
$ 60,000 and trai ling in the Internet estimated at $15,000. The operational costs for Internet
during the life of the project is estimated at about US$175,000.
(c) Short-term internships and study visits: About 40 teacher educators (about 2 from each
institution or about 160 educators during the four year period). would undertake short visits (of
about 3 months duration) to selected institutions in OECD countries (most at link institutions) to
gain experience of teaching and teacher education methods used in other countries. Unit cost is
estimated at $1,500 per person month, plus travel costs of $2,000. The estimated cost for 40
person years of training is S 1.0 million. Another 40 teacher educators per year (total 160) would
visit regional countries for about 4 to 6 weeks over the period of the project. Cost of these 20
visits is estimated at $280,000. Preference in both cases would be given to teacher educators over
45 years of age with at least three years to serve before retirement.
(d) Continuing teacher education: The project would support continuing education for teachers
(US$3.6 million) through NIE, the NCOEs and the TCs. Part of this effort is to be financed by
SIDA, which is already making an important contribution to teahcer education.
(e) Other training activities: (i) An annual conference for teacher educators in country would
be partially financed ($5000 annually for 4 years) under the project; (ii) Staff from teacher
89



education institutions within the country would be paid per diem expenses (up to a total of $4,000
per year for four years) to visit other institutions within the country to observe pilot and other
initiatives; (iii) A three week training course would be designed and delivered in-country for
teacher educators and administrators involved in data collection and analysis and educational
planning techniques; initial technical assistance would be provided on the course design (1
month visit at a cost of $22,500). Total project allocation of $50,000 would cover this technical
assistance and partial course costs (materials, per diem); (iv) Based on a serious shortage of
national teacher education literature and materials, the project would cover the costs of
translation and printing of research reports and theses into Sinhala, Tamil and English. The
costs for these translations is estimated at Rs.50,000 per publication and the project would fund
up to 100 manuscripts/publications for a total cost of $100,000; and (v) The project would
support an annual teacher education writing competition to develop instructional materials to be
used by teacher educators. The fields of competition would cover primary (Sinhala, Tamil,
environment, mathematics) and secondary (science, mathematics, English) and professional
methodology (child psychology, methods of teaching). Financing would provide a prize of up to
Rs.50,000 in each of ten areas annually for a total of $50,000 equivalent over the five years of the
project.
28.    About 12 eminent international teacher educators, with cutting edge credentials would be
identified to offer training in Sri Lanka on the most up-to-date methodology and content available. Each
year, for about 3-4 years these eminent teacher educators would be invited to attend the annual teacher
educator conference and give critical seminars and training sessions to teacher educators and
administrators. About 12 consultant months (12 visits over 4 years for a total of $948,000) would be
financed by the project. The first specialists would, under the coordination of NATE, be identified within
six months of project effectiveness.
29.    Strategies for implementing a staff development plan of this magnitude would include: (i)
devolving responsibility for the selection and approval of candidates to NATE and working out
mechanisms for their implementation; (ii) responsibility for the daily administration of the plan being
handled by the educator within the Project Coordinating Unit (PCU); and (iii) agreeing on criteria for
selection of staff for all types of development opportunities.
Component E: StrenfftheninM and Uneradina of Teacher Trainine Institutions: (estimated baseline
cost US$49.5 million).
30.    The objective of this component would be to: (i) rationalize the number and location of teacher
education institutions to improve regional equity and to meet the projected needs for initial and continuing
education; and (ii) to improve the quality of facilities and equipment. The proposed rationalization would
reduce unit costs of operation, improve access and reduce the proportion of residential facilities required
for initial training. Under the project the existing 31 institutions presently involved in the delivery of
teacher education programs would be reduced to 19 (14 NCOEs, NE and 4 universities). Since many of
the institutions are not located where they are most needed (based on demographic and enrollment data),
and others use rented space or old Second World War army barracks that need to be replaced, it will be
less costly to construct five new institutions than to upgrade existing buildings, in places where national
needs could be better met. Such re-locations would also enable MEHE to increase the number of day
students, thus reducing operation costs. All institutions in satisfactory condition would be retained. Also,
the existing 250 teacher centers would be reduced to 81.
31.    The project would support: (i) rehabilitation and extension of 9 existing COEs, upgrading them
to NCOEs; (ii) construction of 5 new NCOEs; (iii) upgrading of facilities for teacher education at the
Universities of Colombo and Jaffna; (iv) refurbishing, furnishing and equipping 60 TCs/Type A and 3
Type B (TEIs); (v) developing, refurbishing furnishing and equipping a further 18 TCs/Type A within
90



existing facilities (including, as required, 10 existing TTCs); and (vi) provision of furniture and
equipment for 14 NCOEs (including Sariputta), NIE, the Universities of Colombo, Peradeniya, Jaffna and
Open University. ADB is expected to finance refurbishing the 3 Type B TCs (TEIs), providing furniture,
equipment and educational materials. The civil works will be undertaken at existing sites or at sites
already acquired by the Government. All the existing institutions COEs and TTCs (except three which
are too dilapidated or in rented spaces) will be retained either as NCOEs or TCs. The TCs will continue
primarily to conduct courses in existing schools. Details of institutional rationalization is provided in
Annex 22A and 22B.
32.    New NCOEs would be located in urban centers where a large proportion of students could attend
as lower cost day students (many have, for budgetary reasons, adopted this lower cost approach during
recent years). The project would increase the proportion of day students while increasing residential
facilities for females and maximizing the use of currently under-used boarding facilities. Residential
capacity would range from 55-84 percent of student capacity, depending on the institution, with an overall
average of 67 percent.
33.    In order to provide acceptable standards for construction, renovation and maintenance a National
Teacher Education Physical Planning and Building Committee would be established as a standing
committee of NATE. This committee would have representatives from each of the agencies involved in
teacher education, and from the School Buildings Department of MEHE, the provincial departments of
public works and the national architects' association. The committee would prepare and maintain
guidelines detailing standards considered essential for facilities (buildings, furniture and fixtures) to be
used by adults. It would also review the proposed physical planning and lay-outs for different types of
teacher education institutions to ensure that the teacher facilities norms, agreed to during appraisal, are
met.
34.    The physical facilities identified for each institution have resulted from an exercise which
matched the revised/proposed curriculum and the resources/spaces required to achieve these goals.
Detailed education and architectural worksheets have been prepared for each institution and are included
in the Implementation Volume. Thus, the facilities proposed are in response to actual needs and
programs to be offered in each institution. Where suitable facilities exist these will not be replicated.
35.    Since many of the project civil works inputs are at existing institutions the focus would be on
improving existing facilities and increasing responsiveness in order to reach acceptable common
standards. The present capacity of the existing sites would, in most cases, be filly utilized while making
the campus easier to manage. The unit investment cost (civil works, architectural fees, furniture and
equipment) per student would vary from US$1,000 - 4,600 for the existing institutions and about
US$7,400 - 8,100, dependent on site, for the new facilities. Civil works and physical facilities proposals
are listed in Annex 26. These norms are based on spaces used in other IDA-financed projects in Asia
and on the UNESCO recommended average space allocations. Detailed design work for each of the
institutions is being completed and costed by national and IDA consultants (architectural estimates have
been prepared during appraisal on the basis of educational worksheets developed for each institution and
will be available in the implementation volume). The current ADB financed secondary education project,
which also has a teacher training component, covers some of these institutions, and agreement has been
reached on how to coordinate activities.
36.    Each institution will employ one or two full-time maintenance officers. These officers should be
trained, as a pre-requisite for appointment, prior to taking up their duties (preferably in a technical
institute through a special course). The project would include the design and delivery of such a course,
with a duration of about one month, for about 32-40 maintenance officers. As part of the project, each
institution would prepare, by the end of the second year of the project, a comprehensive maintenance plan
with budget requirements (based on criteria developed by the School Construction Unit during the first
year of the project). Upon endorsement of these plans by NATE, a basis for allocation of funds for
91



institutional maintenance would be formulated. The institutions would administer the program, prepare
annual reports with needs and on that basis would receive future annual allocations. In the case of
NCOEs, the delegation to administer the maintenance budget would be part of the overall increase in
financial autonomy, referred to above.
Component F: Strenfthen Management and Adminsitration of Teacher Education Institutions
(estimated baseline cost of US$ 0.6):
37.    Teacher education will be delivered through a nationally coordinated system of post-secondary
institutions; the Project would address their management and funding policies. They will, under the
coordination of NATE and the Chief Commissioner of Teacher Education, be given more opportunities
for self-management, including self-management of their budgets. To assist with this process, training
would be given to institution heads, accountants or registrars and other administrators. The budgets would
be computerized with standard budget line items in all the institutions. The project would support the
review of the system during the first year of the project and offer training to about 20 senior staff and 50
administrative staff. Estimated costs are about $ 50,000 senior staff and $20,000 for administrative staff.
Such training would be offered throughout the life of the project.
38.    Self-management will allow the instutions realistic amounts for daily operation and maintenance
(contrary to the present system where authorization is needed for about every $10.00). Annually, each
institution (including the university Faculties of Education and NIE Teacher Education and Distance
Education Departments) would prepare and submit to NATE a budget following prescribed categories and
agreed norms and unit cost allocations. Once accepted by NATE, these budget lines/items would be
included in the operational budgets of the respective universities, NIE and MEHE (subdivided directly to
each other institution) and be dedicated for use for teacher training. Within that scenario, each institution
will receive every semester about half of its budget (decentralized to the school with increased
accounting). The next semester's allocation would only be made following receipt of the previous
semester's accounting report.
39.    To arrive at that budget allocation stage, two important analyses, under the coordination of
NATE, need to be undertaken during the first year of the project and later reviewed annually. The
analysis would assess all material, teacher support, books, audio visual and library needs (using some
other regional institution allocations as comparators), maintenance and salaries (related to course and
teaching loads and support staff ratios to be established) and determine what resources are required to
effectively operate a NCOE and TC. The budget would then be broken down into the following
categories: (i) new capital inputs to be included in this annual allocation, i.e. furniture and audio visual
equipment and other materials; (ii) education inputs required at the start of each academic year (such as
books, paper, etc.). All costs would be based on a list of essential requirements by program (to be
developed during the first year of the project and which would be supplied by the project and later
sustained on an annual basis by the national budget); (iii) the ongoing expenditures (monthly basis) of
programs offered, to sustain consumable materials, essential needs and develop a strategy of replacement
(progressive manner) of essential teaching materials; (iv) costed lists of essential instructional materials
such as library, textbooks and teaching aids for each program (based on norms); and (v) maintenance
requirements for the physical infrastructure. The other goal is to have, by the end of the project,
institutions which can be self managed and hold their own budgets (as done in similar institutions
internationally). Such self management would thus be based on agreed thresholds and allocated fully as
part of an annual budget clearly related to an agreed unit cost. Thus, the final budgetary allocation would
be determined by the number of trainees trained in each institution. If the number of students is larger or
smaller than the previous semester the budget allocations would be adjusted accordingly.
Studies and Monitorina: (estimated baseline cost of USS 0.3):
Six main studies would be undertaken during the project. Their principal focus would be on monitoring the
impact of the policy changes and resnuctung envisaged under the project, with particular regard to: (i) teacher

teacher education fimding and (v) the effectins of the National Authority on Teacher Education In

Annex 12
SRI LANKA
TEACHER EDUCATION AND TEACHER DEPLOYMENT PROJECT
OUTCOME, COSTS, AND BENEFITS OF PROJECT ACTIVITIES
The main focus for the Project is to rationalize teacher deployment and quality improvements in teacher
education. This would be achieved by addressing access, quality, efficiency, cost-effectiveness and sustainability
of teacher training programs in Sri Lanka. The following analysis is an attempt to assess the project activities'
cost-effectiveness which includes the main actions that would be undertaken, their outcome, and (where possible)
estimnates of their costs and benefits.
The analysis shows that the Project and the programs it supports have a broadly neutral fiscal impact The declining
enrollment in general education (both primary and secondary) due to demographic trends, with the low STR of
24:1 and the excess of teachers in the system, increases the need to rationalize use of education sector resources at
the school, provincial, and central levels. At the same time, the tight fiscal condition and the increasing public
budget deficit further intensify the need to rationalize Government expenditures and, in turn, put more pressure on
the MEHE and the provinces to rationalize teacher numbers and their distribution through recruitment control and
consolidation of small schools.
Teacher employment rationalization, linking application of the mechanism to resource allocations, would generate
substantial sector cost reductions. The summary and detailed tables below show that during the period 1996-2005,
aggregate salary expenditure (using the recent 1995 salary scale) could be reduced by Rs 1.6 billion if teacher
recruitment is controlled as planned, as the total number of teachers and school administrators would be reduced by
25,000 by 2005. If project-related reforms are carried out fully, and the improvement in education progressively
reduces repetition rates substantially, total fiscal savings during the period 1996-2005 could in the best case add
further savings of between Rs 2 and 3 billion, making total savings for the 10 years over Rs 4 billion, or US$74
million, equivalent to the costs of the project and incremental expenditures on teacher training. When the
unquantifiable (but large) benefits from improved levels of general education in the population at large are factored
in, the project benefits are massive. The saving in education salaries would be re-invested in desperately needed
quality components such as school supplies and teaching materials, increased teacher training, and to develop
support and incentive schemes to motivate teacher transfers to remote and hardship areas.

The following table includes the details of project activities, outcome, and costs and benefits. The Project
emphasizes three high priority actions: first, to rationalize the deployment of teachers, linking this to budget
allocations; second, to rationalize and standardize the numbers and content of teacher training programs
including the consolidation, physical upgrading and equitable distribution of the teacher training institutions; and
third, to upgrade the teacher educator staff qualifications to improve the quality of the programs and increase
94



their response and linkages to the school curriculum and to children's needs. The analysis is presented under
five main headings: rationalization of teacher deployment; improving structure and organization of teacher
education; rationalization of teacher education programs; upgrading of staffing and staff development for
teacher education; and rationalization of facilities and equipment of teacher training institutions.

Annex 13
SRI LANKA
TEACHER EDUCATION AND TEACHER DEPLOYMENT PROJECT
TEACHER CADRE COMMITTEE
Context: MEHE, through the Data Processing Branch, determines the cadre entitlement for schools,
based on the Ready Reckoner. School inputs are currently collected by Divisional Education Officers,
and forwarded to MEHE, which checks school entitlements. Based on advice from MEHE, the
Finance Commission incorporates funding provision for salaries into provincial block grants through
the Ministry of Finance. In practice, the cadre entitlements (for each school) within a given province
are used to establish the overall entitlement of that province and do not necessarily affect the actual
staff allocation to individual schools. Proposed changes for the introduction in 1996 (and for use with
MIS) provide for Zones to enter school data and for Provinces to collate Zone inputs, prior to a
random sample check by MEHE.
Project Targets: Teacher recruitment would be control below the attrition and this will lead to a
reduction in the number of teachers and the student:teacher ratio will increase to 26:1 for primary and
22:1 by 2001.
Rationale for Committee: In order to achieve and maintain the project targets, close monitoring
with annual adjustments will be required. The Cadre Comnmittee would broaden the scope for
involvement of interested parties in the application of the Ready Reckoner and the allocation of the
salaries budget for provinces, annually.
Membership: Membership would comprise: (1) the Additional Secretary (Administration), Ministry
of Education and Higher Education (MEHE) chair; (2) a representative of the National Authority for
Teacher Education; (3) two Provincial Directors of Education (Rotate in every three years); (4) a
representative of the Secretary to the Ministry of Provincial Councils; (5) two representatives of the
Secretary to the Ministry of Finance one of whom shall be from the Planning Division and the other
from the Budget Division; (6) Director of Policy, Planning and Review Division, Ministry of
Education; (7) Chairman/Secretary of Education Service Committee; (8) Chief Commissioner of the
Colleges of Education; and (9) Representative of the Finance Commission.
Functions: The principal functions of the Cadre Committee would be as follows;
* to review the annual student and staff projections prepared by the Data Processing Branch, MERE;
* to review and make recommendations to the Secretary, MEHE, on the annual adjustments to the
STR which would be required to meet the project STR targets by year 2000;
* to review the cadre requests, on a province by province basis, against the Ready Reckoner
entitlements;
* to determine annual cadre entitlements and linked salaries budget for each province, together with
any tolerance levels deemed to be appropriate, and to recommend accordingly to the Secretary
MEHE and the Secretary, MOFP;
* to monitor progress towards meeting the project STR targets on a province by province basis and,
if necessary, make recommendations to the Secretary, MEBE on strategies for achieving the
targets within the agreed timeframe,;
* to review the effectiveness of the National Policy on Teachers Transfers in achieving an equitable
distribution of teachers, nationally;
* to advise NATE, annually, on short, medium and long-term projected teacher demand, having
particular regard to requirements by discipline, medium of instruction and provincial distribution;
* to prepare an annual report to the Secretary and Minister, MEHE and the Secretary and Minister
of Finance on the staffing and the salaries budget status of each province in relation to the project
targets.

TOTAL
2. Specific T.A. by Component:
A.       For Rationalization of Teacher Deployment:
This component of the project would support: (i) technical assistance for a period of 12 months of a
national consultant (6 months in the first year of the project, 4 months in the second year, and 2 months
in the third year) to assist in the implementation of the revised RR, immediately following project
effectiveness; (ii) technical assistance for a period of 5 months of international consultant services (3
visits of one month in the first year and 2 visits of one month in the second year) to assist MEHE and the
provinces in data collection and analysis and the application of the RR to achieve the STR targets; and
(iii) technical assistance for a period of 40 person months of a national consultant to work with the
international consultants [(ii) above] in assisting MEHE and the provinces in matters relating to
recruitment, deployment and transfers. The consultants would train staff at all levels.
B.       For Structure and Organization:
I.       Support for NATE would include: (a) international technical assistance for (i ) a consultant
for a period of 4 months (3 months in the first year of the project and I month in the second year) to
advise on the establishment and management of NATE; (ii) a consultant for a period of 4 months (3
months in the first year of the project and I month in the second year) to advise on thc establishment and
operation of the accreditation framework for teacher education programs; (iii) an eminent teacher
105



educator to serve on the Accreditation Standing Committee for a period of up to 4 months ( 5 visits of 3
weeks) during the first 4 years of the project; and
(b) national technical assistance for: (iv) a consultant for a period of 12 months (9 in first year of
project and 3 in second year) to assist institutions in implementing the accreditation system; (v) a
consultant for 1 month to review the operation of the accreditation during the mid-term review of the
project; (vi) a consultant for a period of 6 months (4 in year 1 of the project and 2 in year 2) to establish
an integrated planning model and data base for NATE and teacher education institutions to strengthen the
planning, coordination and management capacity; (vii) a consultant for 4 months (3 months in first year
of project and 1 month in the second year) to review funding requirements for institutions based on a unit
cost for different types of programs.
2.     Support for the Chief Commissioner of Teacher Education would include: (a) visits by 2
members of the Chief Commissioner's Office, to three regional countries (2 x 4 weeks each) to appraise
the operation of similar systems, having particular regard to the allocation of resources and effective
management; (b) international technical assistance for three months (3 x 1 month) to assist in reviewing
the role and functions of the Chief Commissioner and in the development of effective management and
monitoring systems for the Office; and (c) equipment (computer, printer, photocopier and fax/modem).
3.     Support for Institutions: Procurement of equipment (computer, printer, photocopier and
fax/modem, per entity) and furniture for NATE, Universities, NIE, and NCOEs. Funding for a national
publicity campaign on teacher education, resource materials for NATE (for example, books on teacher
education, accreditation, program budgeting in tertiary institutions), and recurrent costs of NATE on a
declining basis up to $60,000.
C.     For Teacher Education Programs
The project would support the following technical assistance, overseas assignment and fellowships as well
as in-country experience in each of the above programs (details are developed in an Implementation
Paper). The majority of such support would occur within the first two years of the project. In summary,
this would require:
(a) about 51 international consultant months ($988,000) for program design and course outline for subject
specialization in initial teacher education and 198 national consultant months (costing about $257,000).
These provisions are expected to be provided under the ADB Secondary Education Development Project;
(b) about 40 international consultant months ( $790,000) foT the design and development of continuing
teacher education programs, about half of which would be assigned to distance education, together with
120 national consultant months (costing $156,000);
(c) about 6 international consultant months ($120,000) with 3 visits of two months each to assist local
consultants in assessing equivalency of Diploma and Certificate Courses and in the design and conduct of
a pilot needs assessment study to identify local teacher course needs. A national consultant team would
assist wkith the local divisional needs analysis and equivalency assessment (10 person months, costing
$ 13,000);
(d) national curriculum developers at N1E would work together with the international consultants and be
allocated 48 staff months to visit institutions within the region and within the country ($28,800);
(e) about 3 international consultant months (costing $62,000) would be required to develop more
streamlined criteria for student selection procedures to NCOEs;
(f) the project would fund ($5,000 per year for four years) an annual series of seminars or "brainstorming"
sessions for teacher education administrators and educators in specialized areas to review and develop
syllabi content for initial and continuing teacher education;
(g) each institution involved in teacher education would be encouraged to propose pilot andlor
experimental activities or initiatives e.g. minor surveys, experiments according to teaching methods in
different subject areas, exhibitions of developed teaching aids. These proposals would be reviewed and
106



approved annually by NATE. NATE will also assign respective institutions to implement the proposals.
The Project would fund implementation of pilot activities and initiatives costing up to a total of $50,000
per year, for four years (total $200,000);
(h) an allocation of about $1.0 million would be provided for the development and printing for distance
education course material for continuing education programs over the five years of the project.

Line responsibility     Integrated national system
Summary of Principal Responsibilities and Functions:
National Authority for Teacher Education: responsible to the Minister, MEHE, for overall policy
development, planning, co-ordination and monitoring of the integrated national teacher education system.
Chief Commissioner for Teacher Education: Responsible to Secretary, MEHE for the effective management
of NCOEs, including finance, staffing, student allocation and facilities, equipment and teaching resources.
National Colleges of Education: Responsible to the Chief Commissioner for Teacher Education, through the
Council, for the delivery of accredited initial and continuing teacher education in accordance with agreed
profiles for each institution. The organisational structure includes Teacher Centres, Type A and Type B
(Teacher Education Institutes), which would be allocated to each NCOE, by MEHE, on the recommendation of
NATE. In the allocation of TCs to NCOE particular attention would be given to demographic and access
factors.
National Institute of Education: Responsible to the Minister, MEHE, under the provisions of the Act, for
curiculum development for initial and continuing education teacher education programs, for the delivery of
selected teacher education programs (generally through the distance education mode), and for the provision of
professional development programs for teacher educators in NCOEs. Teacher education programs would be
subject to accreditation through NATE. In addition, NE would continue its role in curriculum development
for schools.
108



Faculties of Educadon: Responsible to their respective Universities for teaching and research. In selected
universities, which choose to become part of the national integrated teacher education system, Faculties of
Education would offer initial and continuing teacher education programs consistent with agreed profiles and
guidelines negotiated through NATE. Programs would be subject to accreditation through NATE. It is
expected that Faculties of Education would have a major role in post graduate studies and in research relating
to teacher education.

-Annex 16
SRI LANKA
TEACHER EDUCATION AND TEACHER DEPLOYMENT PROJECT
NATIONAL AUTHORITY ON TEACHER EDUCATION
The National Authority on Teacher Education (NATE) would be established as an integral part of the
restructuring of teacher education to form a co-ordinated national system. NATE would be responsible to the
Minister of Education and Higher Education for overall policy development, planning, co-ordination and
monitoring (including accreditation of programs) of the national system of teacher education.
NATE would be:
* a semi-autonomous statutory body,
* responsible to the Minister, Education and Higher Education,
* within the framework of MEHE.
* The functions of NATE would include:
Co-ordination
*  co-ordination of the national system of teacher education
Planning at National Level
* policy development for establishing and maintaining an integrated system of national teacher education;
* designing and promulgating a planning model and a format for data bases;
* rationalising inconsistencies within the existing national system;
* developing a unit cost framework for programs and institutions.
Facilitating Implementation of a National System
* anticipating and addressing potential impediments to implementation of a national system;
* relating teacher demand to supply, including allocation of student numbers by course to institutions;
* collating budget estimates for providing institutions, based on unit cost analysis;
* co-ordinating professional activities among providing institutions;
* co-ordinating assistance from overseas agencies, including Link Institutions;
* co-ordinating and approving scholarship awards;
* establishing criteria for selection and promotion of staff;
* establishing criteria for appointment of heads of institutions
Monitoring and Research
* establishing and maintaining mechanisms for accreditation of training programs;
* reviewing student intakes, progress and outputs (relating to demand);
* reviewing expenditure patterns and unit cost;
* promoting and co-ordinating research activities relating to teacher education;
* initiating and co-ordinating follow-up and appraisal of activities.
Public Information on Teacher Education
* designing publicity and promulgating information on teacher education;
* promoting the publication and circulation of reports (eg., theses and study visit reports).
110



NATE Relationship with the Office of the Chief Commissioner for Teacher Education:
* NATE would be the policy, co-ordination, and accreditation authority, and
*  Thc Chief Commissioner for Teacher Education would continue to be responsible for the administration
and supervision of the teacher education institutions.
Proposed Structure of NATE:
* a governing council: representatives to include MEHE, NEC, UGC, Finance Commission, two Provincial
Directors of Education, Universities, NIE, NCOEs, TCs, Schools, Teacher Educator Service, NATE;
* a part-time Chairman appointed by the Minister, Education and Higher Education;
* two Deputy Chairmen, at least one with a background in teacher education - with provision for rotation;
* a full-time secretariat.
Standing Committees would include:
* Course Accreditation;
- Staff Development and Scholarship Awards (including Link Institutions);
- Resource Allocation and Monitoring;
- Teacher Demand, Supply and Student Enrolment and Progression;
- Physical Facilities, Buildings and Equipment.
Staffing for NATE would comprise:
 a full-time director (director-general) ex-officio member of NATE Council;
e three full-time professional officers;
 five administrative support staff;
* provision for secondment from time to time.

Annex 20
SRI LANKA
TEACHER EDUCATION AND TEACHER DEPLOYMENT PROJECT
Continuing Education Programs
1.     In today's society, continuing education is extremely important within all professions. The
amount of knowledge is changing and increasing all the time. A basic education or graduation cannot
last for a professional career. A person with a basic education or graduation has to be up-graded,
broadened, refreshed and even re-trained to adjust to new developments within the society. This is also
valid for teachers. What is supposed to be taught in the classrooms is changing continually.
2.     To enable teachers to remain conversant with modem trends and subject content, MEHE has
decided to expand its in-service education provincial programs and to offer more comprehensive
continuing education to all teachers in Sri Lanka. This project proposes four types of continuing
education: upgrading, broadening, retraining and refreshing. All four are equally important. These
types may be offered through distance (mixed) self-learning mode, regular contact courses or sessions, and
intensive residential courses.
3.     The basic concept of offering a broad range of continuing education programs for teachers is
essential if Sri Lankan schools are to improve their quality. Therefore, within this project, funding is
provided for the development and delivery of the four different types of continuing education:
(a) The upgrading courses would keep teachers up-to-date in subject content and methodology by
providing structured courses which would (i) largely fulfill the requirements of the Teachers Service
Minute, and (ii) allow untrained, partially trained and Basic Certificated teachers to qualify for a Diploma
in Teaching equivalent to the NCOE award. These courses would be offered through a combination of
distance learning mode and intensive face-to-face training (both residential and non-residential). For
teachers who have completed Basic Training only through distance mode, an intensive residential
component of three weeks duration would be required, rather than further distance mode training. Such
residential upgrading would be conducted in Teacher Centres (Type BlTEIs) and in NCOEs. It is
intended that project funds would be used by NIE to develop and print the 15 modules for distance
education (which would also be the basis for the three week intensive residential alternative. Such
residential courses would give preference to those teachers who had not received previous residential-
based training.).
(b) The broadening courses would encourage teachers to expand their knowledge and skills in order to
obtain additional qualifications. Courses would continue to be offered by universities and NIE, leading to
recognized awards. This project would (i) expand the range of courses available by funding the
preparation of undergraduate level distance mode courses to be identified by NATE; (ii) finance the
preparation of specialised regular contact courses; and (iii) assist in financing the organization and
administration of continuing education. NCOEs and Teacher Centres (Type A) could also be used for the
contact portions of the distance mode courses.
(c) The re-training courses would (i) allow teachers to adapt their area of specialization to meet particular
demands for specific subject teachers, and (ii) continue the provincial in-service training which could
satisfy some of the requirements of the Teachers Service Minute. Project funding would only be used for
the former; such specialized study could be taken on a full-time or part-time basis. The need for such re-
training is expected to diminish as more teachers are prepared initially (pre-service) in accordance with
identified subject demand.
117



(d) The refeshing activities would cater to the identified needs of local teachers. Such local needs will be
identified through provision of technical assistance, and training would be managed and conducted at
minimal costs through short sessions (half day to two days) given in TCs and/or in schools. Such
activities would, for example, introduce teachers to revised and new programs and strengthen the
professional identity of teachers. Refreshing activities would be contact sessions in the form of workshops
or seminars. One of their purposes is to fulfill local needs, consequently the content of the refreshing
seminars would vary from one area to the other. Another purpose is to strengthen the teacher's identity
and for that purpose the social component of meeting together in groups is very important. Refreshing
activities would not lead to any formally recognized award, although they may, over time, become
recognized for purposes of the Teachers Service Minute.

4.      The project proposes to fund only portion of the above Continuing Education program and should
not be seen as covering the costs of fulfilling the requirements of the Teachers Service Minute. The
intention is to expedite the development of distance mode modules and their delivery, and to cover the
administration anm organizational costs for a limited number of teachers in each of the four types of
Continuing Education. The costs of continuing the existing provincial in-service contact training would
not be supported by the project. The following estimated costs, covered by the project, are intended also
to give an indication of unit costs for each type of activity:

DEIC : Developmat and printing of fifeen Distance Education modules, administration and at least one contact session per module
IR: Intsive Residential course of three weeks duration
WEID: Weekend and day sessios in local schools or TCs
Ddails of the possible scope of each Type and of the methodology for deriving these costs are provided in an Implementation Paper.
5.     The curriculumn for continuing education has to be very flexible. It should be the framework
within which the teachers have a possibility to adapt and adjust their knowledge and skills in accordance
with scientific developments and with development within the society. Initially, the content of the courses
would be based on (i) the outcome of the needs assessments and (ii) the requirements of the Teachers
Service Minute. For upgrading and retraining courses, programs would be designed to cover methodology
and subject areas where the teachers are teaching or want to teach. For broadening courses, there would
be other programs as well, such as health and nutrition, gender issues, computer science, languages and
new knowledge within the professional area. For refresher courses, the main purpose is to cater to local
needs identified by the teacher, parents, pupils and the local community. In a long term perspective, all
institutions involved in teacher education should be involved in developing ideas for continuing education
courses of all types. These ideas would be sent to NATE for evaluation and selection. The selected ideas
would be assigned by NATE for further development, processing, and implementation by NIE, NCOEs, or
universities.
6.     NATE will be responsible for the coordination of the needs and delegation of the development of
course material and course design to NIE, universities or NCOEs. The project would provide TA to assist
in training of staff who would be responsible for course layout/design and development of the distance
education self-instructional material. TA would assist in designing the set-up necessary (including
infrastructure, logistical delivery, monitoring mechanism and training of on-site tutors and facilitators) to
meet the demands of continuing education in general and distance education in particular. In total , 40
international consultant months are assigned for design and development of continuing education
programs, about half of which are proposed for distance education. There would also be 120 national
consultant months.
7.     Distance education will be used as one of the delivery modes in three of the four types of
continuing education. The Department of Distance Education and the Department of Teacher Education
within NIE as well as Open University are at present offering courses that can be classified mainly as
upgrading and broadening courses by means of distance education. These courses can and should be
continued in the new program of continuing education. Examples are B.Ed., Dip. Ed. and M.Ed.
upgrading courses offered by the Department of Teacher Education, NIE and Open University; the Basic
Certifciation courses (which could be extended to Diploma) and some broadening courses (e.g., English,
Tamil and Sinhala as a second language) offered by the Department of Distance Education, NIE. The
basic and broadening courses offered by means of Distance Education at the Department of Distance
Education, NIE, are currently funded by SIDA. The agreement made between SIDA and Sri Lanka is
effective through December 1998.
8.     The project's teacher education programs include both initial and continuing education activities
in order to enhance the quality of education. The linkages between both programs will be better
coordinated to ensure that teachers can improve their qualifications through one or a combination of
initial and continuing training courses. To make sure that the content of the upgrading, broadening and
re-training courses is suitable and supports teacher improvement, a cross-creditation of such courses will
be undertaken by NATE. However, refreshing sessions and other short courses would not be included in
such cross-creditation.

TEACHER EDUCATION AND TEACHER DEPLOYMENT PROJECT
National Colleges of Education Staffing
Staffing Assumptions and Allocation:
In order to maximize the use of academic staff in each institution, the following assumptions have been made
regarding likely subject combinations for staff teaching:
a.     Health & Personal Hygiene can be linked with Physical Education & Sports.
b.     Science, Agriculture, Aesthetics (Art, Music, Dance, Drama), Home Science, Technology/Technical
Studies staff teach both theory and practical sessions.
c.     Science and Math can be linked, if necessary.
d.     Language, Health, Aesthetics, Library staff will teach in the General, Professional Methods of Teaching
and the Specialized Area.
e.     Staff teaching Sociology of Education could also teach Sri Lankan Society.
f.     Educational Psychology could, if needed, be linked with Evaluation & Measurement as well as with
Guidance & Counselling.
g.     All academic staff should be involved in supervision of practice teaching and observation. Those staff
teaching in the Specialization Area should be more heavily involved in supervising students in the
internship year.
h.     Elements of Education should be linked with School & Classroom Organization.
The overall basis for staffing assumes a teaching or contact load of 14-17 sessions per week per academic staff
member.
Abbreviations used in the Worksheets are:

ED=Education/Methods          PS=Psychology                  SO=Sociology
LI=Library                    MA=Maths                      PE=Health& Physical Education
PR=Primary                    SC=Science                    TE=Technical Studies

in the Educational Worksheets which show contact periods per week and space requirements.
