Annex 23
SRI LANKA
TEACHER EDUCATION AND TEACHER DEPLOYMENT PROJECT
Criteria for Staff Development
Criteria for Appointment of Heads of Teacher Education Institutions
The following are some of the general criteria which need to be considered in the open selection of heads,
administrators or department heads of teacher education institutions. This list needs to be
modified/elaborated on from time to time:
* Demonstrated ability as a teacher, and p-referably as a teacher educator
*  Ability to identify problems, consider a%ernative solutions and to make decisions based on
substantiated evidence.
* Demonstrated ability to play an active role in preparing and implementing institutional plans
and programs.
* Knowledge of, and ability to implement, management principles and techniques for
increasing the effectiveness and efficiency of an institution.
* Demonstrated experience in working effectively with others, in molding teams and in
professional leadership.
*  Proven ability to work with other managers/senior administrators within the relevant
authorities responsible for teacher education, and with members of government
boards/councils.
* Strong academic qualifications (preferably a Master's degree), and evidence of involvement
in professional bodies.
* Professional qualifications in education, and preferably in teacher education or management.
* Effective personal and communication skills with adults.
* Personality characteristics, social skills, and community participation/contribution which
will enhance effective leadership.
Criteria for Appointment of Staff as Teacher Educators
The following are some of the general criteria which need to be considered in the open selection of teacher
educators. This list needs to be modified/elaborated from time to time:
* Ability to think critically and creatively and to guide others in the learning process.
* Minimum of five years' experience in teaching at the level (primary or secondary) and in the
discipline/subject to which he/she will be assigned in the institution.
* Specialized knowledge in his/her subject field or professional/pedagogical area.
*  Minimum academic qualifications of a Bachelor's degree and Post-Graduate Diploma,
preferably in Education; except for some specialist subject teachers (for example: art, music,
technical studies, physical education) who have had no opportunity to obtain higher
academic awards.
* Demonstrates competence and effectiveness in his/her teaching and in relationships with
others, including desirable values and attitudes.
* Shows a commitment to teaching and to facilitating learning.
* Evidence of involvement in on-going professional development.
126



Criteria for the Selection of Candidates for Staff Development
a)      For Long-Term Fellowships:
*   Requiring academic degree/diploma in a specialized field or discipline to be able to teach
subject content at post-secondary level.
*   Requiring professional degree or diploma at the relevant level.
*   Below the age of 45 years at the time of selection.
*   Demonstrates mental ability and academic study habits suitable for further rigorous
advanced level study.
*   As a teacher educator, contributes significantly to the life and activities of the institution
*   Meets the criteria for a teacher educator, including teaching experience in schools.
*   Demonstrates potential for effective career in teacher education, either as a staff member or
administrator.
*   Able to obtain acceptance by a tertiary institution acceptable to the employing authority.
*   Prepared to contribute to raising the quality and efficiency of their institution
b)      For Short-Term Internship or Assignment:
*   Demonstrates ability to contribute significantly to the life of the institution.
*   Shows willingness to learn through such an internship and to assist other staff on return.
*   Can propose specific activities, research, teaching or related experiences which he/she
wishes to undertake during the internship/assignment directly relevant to his responsibilities
and duties in the institution.
*   Prepared to disseminate knowledge and skills gained following his/her return.

Annex 24
SRI LANKA
TEACHER EDUCATION AND TEACHER DEPLOYMENT PROJECT
TEACHER EDUCATOR STAFF DEVELOPMENT
In the revised system of teacher education, staff in all institutions conducting teacher education programs will need
training. Such training will vary from a few days or weeks observation to several years' full-time study leading to
recognized degrees. A training plan should be developed by the Project Coordinating Unit and NATE to cover
nearly all teacher educators in all institutions (universities, NIE, NCOEs and TCs).
ANALYSIS OF ACADEMIC CHARACTERISTICS
The initial step, which must be continually up-dated, has been to identify the academic characteristics of a large
sample (about 87 percent -- from all but one university and one COE) of staff employed in institutions in 1995.
The data collected on 613 teacher educators have been partially analysed and indicate that:
*     38 percent of the respondents were under 45 years of age in 1995; these are the only staff eligible for long-
term further education. They, and other staff not surveyed or yet to be appointed, should form the data base for on-
going analysis to prepare a staff development plan for long-term study. The remaining staff (over 45 years) should
be given opportunities for short-term study and observation.
Of this group of over 200 teacher educators, the following numbers indicate the potential magnitude of training
which may be required for existing academic staff:
Staff requiring              Staff under 45         Staff over 45
First degree                         29(5%)         73(12%)
Diploma in Education(with BA)        3 3(5%)        47(8%)
Diploma in Education(with MA)        25(4%)         25(4%)
Miasters' Degree                     116(20%)       153(24%)
Post-Masters' study                  30(5%)         66(11%)
*     65 percent of staff consider that their first degree (major subject), and 16 percent that their Masters'
degree field, is not relevant to the subjects which they teach in teacher education institutions. This needs to be
investigated further to determine whether adjustments in teaching duties would make greater use of existing
expertise. Some re-training may be needed. Following any re-assignments, a more detailed examination will be
needed of whether any of the remaining teacher educators should receive training in a different discipline.
*     40 percent of the teacher educators are not able to speak or write in English. This would hamper the
possibilities for study abroad. If any of these are in the eligible group, they should be offered training within the
country.
FURTHER ANALYSIS
Additional analyis is required of the existing sample data:
*      correlate the responses to each part of question 11 with those of question 13
*      correlate responses to questions 13 and 14
*      analyse the subjects/disciplines obtained in their degree with those which they now teach and propose
adjustments in teacher education teaching assignments accordingly
*      analyse those lecturers who were teachers, to determine at what level and subject specialisation they
taught, whether these teaching experiences are most relevant to their teacher educator duties and propose
adjustments accordingly
*      seek data on which lecturers have teaching experience at the primary level and correlate this with their
academic qualifications and their current teacher educator teaching responsiblities.
128



*      obtain data from senior administrators in each institution to determine their specific training
requirements, especially for short management and financial training in country.
Once the Project becomes effective, and as new staff (including those in Teacher Centres) are appointed, this data
base will need to be up-dated continually so that an annual analysis can be made.
PREPARING A STAFF DEVELOPMENT PLAN
The two major categories for staff development, whether in-country or abroad, are: (i) fellowships for long-term
study; and (ii) short-term assignments and attachments. Criteria for eligibility (Annex 23) for both categories
need to be refined and agreed as soon as possible. The following steps will need to be taken:
For Long-term Fellowships:
1.     Up-date and verify the numerical data with the actual individual responses through a print out of the
coded data base of the teacher educators who are under 45 years of age. This is best done by institution,
since these data bases will later need to be compared with the recommended priorities submitted by the
heads of each institution.
2.     The recommendations from heads of institutions for priority consideration should be assessed by:
a. comparing the data base for those under 45 with the priority ranked
recommendations and assign a new rank order within each institution;
b. group this new rank-ordered sub-set into levels of formal study (First degree, Post-Graduate Dip.Ed,
Post-Graduate, Other) and prepare a new sub-set across all institutions;
c. verify from both the heads' recommendations and the data base, that this new sub-set is
accurate;
3.     Establish this new sub-set by level as the basis for determining eligibility for study in-country, in-region
and ex-region.
4.     Prepare a list of each sub-set, according to the location proposed for study.
5.     Determine, in consultation with NATE and appropriate authorities, the most appropriate levels and
specific institutions at each training location for each nominated teacher educator.
6.     Prepare a time schedule for each teacher educator to begin a fellowship. Obtain agreement from the
nominee. For those nominees scheduled to commence study during the first two years of the project (late
1996-1997), this detailed schedule should be presented to IDA or the funding agency no later than at the
time of formal project negotiations.
7.     For those persons nominated for study commencing in 1996, initiate discussions with the institution
where study is proposed to obtain admission and other logistical requirements.
8.     Obtain the required approvals from within Government and IDA or other funding agency by March 1996
for each nominee for 1996-1997.
9.     Make appropriate logistical arrangements for each nominees' study whether at home or abroad.
Short-term Assignments:
1.     From the prioritized lists prepared by each head of institution, initially select 50 percent of candidates for
short-term assignment or attachment.
2.     Rank order these candidates according to their eligibility to meet the agreed criteria (see Annex 23),
irrespective of the institution in which they serve.
3.     Group candidates according to type of experience and/or possible location of attachment.
4.     Prepare, by the time of negotiations, an initial list of about 40 candidates intended to be offered
attachments during 1996-1997, grouped by location.
5.     Initiate discussions with possible recipient institutions and determine conditions and timing for each
group.
6.     Obtain concurrence of candidates, and approval from appropriate authorities.
7.     Finalise all arrangements and begin assignments.
129



During negotiations a detailed staff plan and a schedule prepared by MEHE were reviewed and a revised plan will
be included in the implementation volume.

Annex 26
SRI LANKA
TEACHER EDUCATION AND TEACHER DEPLOYMENT PROJECT
STUDIES AND MONITORING
Funding assumption: 515,000 per month plus 55,000 travel (national inputs would cost less).
Six studies would be undertaken during the course of the project. Five of the studies would relate directly to
monitoring the progress and impact of policy initiatives and associated strategies which are central to the effective
implementation of the project. One study (which could comprise a number of smaller studies) would focus on the
investigation of areas which could have relevance to the planning of a future project. The outlines for the proposed
studies are as follows:
1. ImDact of Rationalization of Teacher Denloyment Policies
Purpose: to review the impact of agreed policies and strategies for teacher deployment on resource allocation, the
equitable staffing of schools, and appraise the effectiveness of criteria for teacher progression and promotion.
Scope:
M review of staff cadres by school, district, zone and province;
* analysis of teaching staff deployment by subject and medium of instruction;
e analysis of staff deployment to non-congenial and difficult schools, including years of service and gender, and
related allowances;
e assessment of overall teacher demand and supply projections against staffing formula (Ready Reckoner);
e analysis of deployment of non-teaching staff;
e determine level of salaries saving resulting directly from implementation of changes to deployment policy;
* critical appraisal of criteria for teacher progression and promotion.
Timeframe: up to four months - to be undertaken in years 2 and 4 of the project.
Responsibility: The Cadre Conunittee would be responsible for oversighting the conduct of the study and for the
collection and collation of relevant data.
Consultant Expertise: to include (i) proven capacity to work with senior administrative, planning and finance
personnel; (ii) extensive experience in matters relating to teacher demand and supply and to the operation of
Government systems for teacher employment, deployment, progression and promotion; (iii) knowledge of data
bases for teacher information; (iv) record of achievement in working to agreed deadlines; (v) high level of skill
in spoken and written English.
Estimated Cost: up to $70,000.
2. Trainee Access, Progression, Repetition and Attrition
Purpos: monitor patterns of student access, progression, repetition and attrition and to appraise
resource and service implications.
Scope:
* apply to both initial training and continuing education;
* examination of resource implications of patterns of progression, repetition and attrition in initial training;
* analysis of access patterns for continuing education in direct, distance and residential modes.
Timeframe: up to three months, during second half of project, preferably years 3 and 5.
Responsibility: NATE would be responsible for oversighting the conduct of the study and for collection and
collation of data.
Consultant Expertise: to include (i) proven capacity to work with senior administrative and academic personnel;
(ii) competence in the design and conduct of interviews and surveys, in the use of data analysis techniques
132



(including establishing data bases on student-related information), and in unit cost analyses; (iii) record of
achievement in working to agreed deadlines; (iv) high level of skill in spoken and written English.
Estimated Cost: up to $50,000.
3. Professional DeveloDment of Teachers - Continuin2 Education
Purpose: to identify professional development needs of teachers, as the basis for designing relevant continuing
education programs, and to monitor and appraise the impact of such programs.
Scope:
Phase 1:
* pilot study of five zones to design and test the feasibility of methodology for assessing teacher needs for
continuing education, as required under the Teaching Service Minute;
* national study of the perceived needs of teachers, based on methodology developed in the pilot study, to identify
relevant areas for professional development.
Phase 2:
* analysis of participation rates and attendance patterns;
* appraisal of relationship of identified needs to identified continuing education programs (Phase l);
* analysis of operation and utilization of locations by different agencies;
*  examination of resource utilization, including unit costs;
* appraisal of impact of teacher access to continuing education on quality of teaching;
* analysis of relationship between continuing education and requirements under Teaching Service Minute and
impact on progression within the service.
Timeframe: up to five months, with Phase 1 being undertaken during the first year of the project and Phase 2 in
years 3 and 5 of project.
Responsibility: NATE would be responsible for oversighting the conduct of the study and for collection and
collation of required data.
Consultant Expertise: to include (i) experience in the field of continuing (inservice) education for teachers;
(ii) proven capacity to work with senior administrative and academic personnel; (iii) competence in the design
and conduct of interviews and surveys, in the use of data analysis techniques (including establishing a data bases
on teacher needs), and in unit cost analyses; (iii) record of achievement in working to agreed deadlines; (iv) high
level of skill in spoken and written English.
Estimated Cost: up to $70,000
4. Teacher Education Fundin2
Scope:
* analysis of recurrent expenditure, with item breakdown (eg., salaries, residential, maintenance;
* review of student stipend cost and private costs for teacher education trainees;
* analysis of unit costs of programs, including differences in types of institutions, programs and modes of
delivery;
* review of institutional budget systems and accountability.
Timeframe: up to three months in second half of project.
Responsibility: NATE would be responsible for oversighting the conduct of the study and for the collection and
collation of required data.
Consultant Expertise: to include (i) proven capacity to work with senior admninistrative and academic personnel;
(ii) extensive experience in financial analysis in education, preferably in tertiary contexts; (iii) familiarity with
international practice for determining student:staff ratios, involving full-time and part-time students and direct,
distance and residential modes; competence in use of data analysis techniques (including unit cost program
costing and analysis by program and student; (iii) record of achievement in working to agreed deadlines; (iv)
high level of skill in spoken and written English.
Estimated Cost: up to $55,000.
133



5. Effectiveness of NATE and National System of Teacher Education
Purpose: to review the effectiveness of NATE and integrated national system for teacher education and to make
recommendations on any changes in structure, function or modus operandi that may be required.
Scope:
* appraisal of performance against stated functions for each agency;
* appraisal of relationship among agencies;
* review of data base network;
* review of system resource needs, distribution, utilization and accountability;
* advice on need for any modification of structure, functions or modus operandi.
Timeframe: up to three months - in year 3 and year 5 of project.
Responsibility: an independent Steering Committee, appointed by the Minister, MEHE, and convened through the
Project Co-ordinating Unit, would be responsible for oversighting the study.
Consultant Expertise: to include (i) extensive experience in senior executive positions, preferably including co-
ordinating bodies; (ii) proven capacity to work with senior administrative and academic personnel; (iii) strong
analytical expertise, particularly in relation to appraising effectiveness in terms of policy, planning, and co-
ordination in education context; (iv) record of achievement in working to agreed deadlines; (v) high level of skill
in spoken and written English.
Estimated Cost: up to $55,000.
6. Study of Oualitv Needs
Purpose: to undertake a review/analysis of the quality needs required by grade, subject and classroom to ensure
sufficient quality inputs at the primary, secondary and collegiate levels. The goal would be to identify, under the
co-ordination of NIE the essential and optional quality inputs, establish lists and develop individual school
strategies to meet these goals. The analysis would develop, by level, unit cost requirement for the supply of the
essential and optional quality inputs (per student, classroom, teacher). It would also determine mechanisms to
monitor the allocation, the use and replenishment of the quality inputs. The analysis would compare the quality
inputs in about four other countries, in the region, and ensure that the best potential allocations are arrived at.
Specific lists of quality inputs would be prepared and these would be monitored by the provinces annually.
Timeframe: Within six months after project effectiveness.
Responsibility: MEHE and NIE.
Expertise: National consultants knowledgeable in curriculum and essential educational materials, equipment etc.
needed to effectively teach the various subjects and effectively equip students, teachers and classrooms and
laboratories.
Estimated Costs: US$20,000.
7. Project Preparation
Purpose: to undertake investigations in areas which have the potential for inclusion in a future project.
Scope: possible scope of study/studies to include primary, secondary and tertiary levels, curriculum and
assessment, resources, infrastructure, management, staff development and finance.
Thmeframe: up to 5 months - allocated according to selected range of investigation.
Respondbility: initially through the Project Co-ordinatmg Unit.
Consultant Expertise: dependent on selected areas for investigation.
Estimated Cost: up to $70,000.

Annec 27-0

Annex 29
SRI LANKA
TEACHER EDUCATION AND TEACHER DEPLOYMENT PROJECT
Government Procurement Capacity
1.     Government capacity to handle the procurement proposed under the project is stiUl weak although
improving. All tenders undertaken for education have been decentralized to a MEHE tender committee.
In the past that tender committee suffered from inefficiencies and duplication of services resulting in long
delays with the preparation of tender documentation and bid reviews. The delays were largely caused by
the multiple levels of review and the numerous tender and technical committees (a minimum of two per
tender and staffed with different persons who met separately) with the result that MEHE took on average
8 to 12 months to process a tender. That followed by the delivery period which lasted from six months to
over one year resulting in most procurement activities taking close to two year to complete. The tenders
also suffered from external political pressures making procurement a difficult task.
2.     Following discussions undertaken during the implementation of the ongoing General Education
Project MEHE has agreed to the following adjustments which would be used during the proposed project:
a) to replace the temporary and multiple tender and technical committees by a permanent tender
committee and to establish three or four permanent technical committees (area and subject
based). Both committees (tender and technical) would meet jointly thus reducing the time lag for
tender preparation and tender analysis. The joint conunittee would also be given time limits for
each processing step.
b) The IDA Bidding documentation would be used for all ICB tenders and the provisional NCB
tenders prepared by ICTAD would be for used for all the NCB tenders.
c) MEHE has agreed to establish procurement preparation and review calendars which would
respect the tender periods listed in the bidding documentation. Thus, on the basis that he above
proposed measures it is believed that the MEHE, with some national technical assistance will
have the capacity to undertake the required project procurement activities.
3.     To achieve the above the Project Coordination Unit (PCU) would be staffed with a director, an
architect (with procurement and tender processing experience) and an trained procurement officer. These
posts should be filled prior to or at a minimum by project effectiveness to ensure timely implementation of
the large tender and procurement actions required. The MEHE/School Works Service would assist with
the recruitment of technical staff for the project.
4.     Tenders for civil works would be tendered using: (a) International Competitive Bidding (ICB)
for all works related to the construction and the rehabilitation and expansion of the NCOEs and
renovation works for the University of Jaffna; (b) National Competitive Bidding (NCB) for all works
under US$300,000 (related to the refurbishment and expansion of the Colombo Faculty of Education and
for the instaUation or the nation-wide refurbishment/installation of the TCs type A); and (c) using three
bids for smal refurbishment and rehabilitation contracts
5.    In conformity with the agreements made during appraisal the following bidding procedures will
be used: for all procurement using ICB: (a) IDA standard bidding documentation will be used for civil
works and equipment; (b) all procurement documentation will be standardized and coordinated by PCU in
consultation with the permanent tender and technical teams; and (c) that, tenders only be called folowing
IDA review of the tender documentation packages. For all procurement under NCB: standard
documentation agreed to by IDA (draft ICTAD bidding documentation) would to be used and in that
context the PCU/School Works would: (i) provide provincial services with standard documentation that
141



would have to be used; and (ii) retain an overview during the implementation period to ensure timely
processing.
6.     The PCU will coordinate and have an overview of all project procurement activities (tenders,
contracts and payments for architectural and technical studies, furniture, equipment, books, education
materials, printing contracts, technical assistance, training and studies) utilizing the IDA guidelines and
in accordance with the procurement threshold outlined in Annex 25. All ICB tender documentation will
require a prior IDA review and for the NCB the initial tender documentation (or if substantive changes
are made to later tenders) would be reviewed and commented by IDA prior to tenders.. PCU will be the
contact office for IDA during project implementation.
7.     To assist PCU with the process the procurement activities funds have been included in the project
for the services of national and international procurement specialists.

Annex 34
SRI LANKA
TEACHER EDUCATION AND TEACHER DEPLOYMENT PROJECT
IDA SUPERVISION PLAN
1.     Progress Reviews and Reporting: The Ministry of Education and Higher Education would
assume the implementation, monitoring and reporting responsibilities for this project. These tasks would
largely be delegated to the project coordination unit (PCU) which would assume the day-to-day overview
of the project. PCU would also prepare the monthly status report required by the External Resources
Department and summarize these into semester reports for IDA in December and June of each year
starting December 1996. Based on the experience of the ongoing General Education Project, the report
would include financial and data tables and status summaries using formats suitable for both the
Government and IDA. This joint effort would reduce paper work and result in consistency of reporting
and facilitate the gradual transfer of supervision responsibilities to the IDA Resident Mission Staff in
Colombo starting the second year of project implementation.
2.     The progress reports would include the following: summary of implementation progress (write-
up and tables) listing the status of each project component and comparing it with the plans; financial
summary by component (including funds spent, committed, actual commitments versus planned and
proposals for the next semester); update of the implementation schedule, project implementation plan and
indicators (showing actual versus planned); list of issues and problems that have arisen and proposal of
options for their resolution; data table on activities (planned, actual, proposed for the next with estimated
funding needs) of such activities as civil works, training, fellowships, studies and technical assistance; and
finally, the status of credit disbursements. Every semester the report would assess if the project objectives
are still realistic and advise if new circumstances (political or administrative) are affecting the
implementation of the project goals as set-out at the time of appraisal. The joint reporting format will be
finalized during the start-up seminar.
3.     IDA would review the progress of the project a minimum of twice yearly and if possible three
times yearly. One of these mission would be a more comprehensive annual review during which all
aspects of the project would be closely reviewed. During the first review of each year a joint mission
would be undertaken with the other Donors contributing to the project. A mid-term review is scheduled
about 2 years after project effectiveness, (about July 1998) at which time the project objectives would be
closely reviewed and needed adjustments to the project content and implementation steps would be
undertaken.
4.     The proposed project would be monitored and evaluated from the perspectives of inputs, process,
outputs and impact. The input evaluation would focus on whether the required resources are in place to
implement the program of activities and services. Input information would be monitored and assessed
continuously (reported quarterly, semi-annually "semester reports" and annually) to identify the delivery
input so that problems could be resolved in a timely manner. The process evaluation would examine the
approaches used in the training, service delivery and recipient participation and review the levels of
performance comparable to project inputs and suggest remediation of non-responsive inputs. The output
evaluation would focus on the immediate results of activities, as demonstrated, for examples
improvements of exam results in schools where the qualifications of teachers have been improved etc..
The output evaluation would focus on the program outputs in the terms of programs and review such
factors as: the number to trainees per programs; if the equitable distribution of trained teachers is
improving; whether student teacher ratios are being adjusted; and linkages between the budget and cadre
allocations within each province.
S.     The above evaluation steps would be supplemented by studies (outlined in annex 23). These
studies would assess the impact of the teacher educational and teacher deployment policies being
150



implemented. Since this is a very technical project supervision by IDA staff should be guided by a
experienced educator supported by an education economist who would assess the project's progress. In
view of the large civil works activities in this project, during the annual review the latter specialists should
also be assisted by an architect (first year external specialist and afterwards by national specialists).
6.      The IDA project supervision would be allocated an annual average of 16 staff weeks for in-
country and desk supervision of this project. However, the number of staff weeks required during the first
two years would be about 20 reducing to about 12 during the third and fourth years of implementation. It
is estimated that about half or 8 staff weeks would be used in-country and the other half doing desk work
related to the project:

Selected Documentation in the Project File
A. Reports Related to the Sector:
a) National Education Comission Report, by the National Education Cornission August 1995.
b) Ministry of Education and Higher Education Census Report (Education Statistics) 1994.
c) Education and Training Sector - Strategy Review, Sector Report by the World Bank June
1994.

Prof. L. Jayatilleke, 1995.
e) Study of Education Employment Linkages: Strategies for Linking Education and Training to
the Lobor market. Findings and Recommendations by Marga Institute, 1992
f) Education and Development Project, Appraisal Report, by ADB, April 1991
B. Reports and Studies Related to the Proiect:
a) Reports on First and Second National Teacher Workshops in Sri Lanka (January 1994 and
1995).
b) Action Plan for the Development of Teacher Education, by the Ministry of Education and
National Institute of Education (NIE), May 1994.
c) Teacher Attendance/Absenteeism Study, by NIE, December 1995.
d) Developing Distance Education and Handbook for Distance Education by S.D.
Amaragunasekarra, 1995.
f) Teacher Recruitment and Salaries by M. Allak, 1994.
g) Initial and Continuing Education of Teachers by Mendis and al, 1994.
h) Cost Efffectiveness of Distance Education for Teacher Training by Harvard Bridges Study in
1992.
C. Selected Working Papers;
a) Teacher Education Analysis and project preparation reports completed in December 1995
i) Curricula, Equipement and Books by Ranaweera and al.
ii) Costs and Financing of Teacher Education by Sterling Perrera and M. Kumerage.
iii) Physiscal Facilities of Teacher Training Institutions by Build Environment
Consultants.
iv) Staffing and Staff Development by E. L. Wijemana.
v) Rationalization of Teacher Colleges by D. Guneratne
b) Polices and Strategies for Teacher Education and Teacher Deployment in Sri Lanka by the
World Bank and Ministry of Education and Higher Education, June 22, 1995.
c) Sector Study on Cost, Financing and Policy of Education in Sri Lanka, by Mingat and al,
Institut de Rcserche sur l'Economie de l'Education U of Dijon, France, December 1995

Assumptions and Notes:
1- Data for 1994 was obtained by the mission (October 1995) from MEHE. Teacher education cost is 6% of MEHE budget and 3.3% of total education budget
2- Cost projections are based on 1994 unit costs and on expected capacity needs.
3- The proposed rationalization includes the conversion of the COEs and TTCs into NCOEs
4- The basic distance teacher education program will be reduced by 1998 when the backlog of untrained
teachers currently in training will be completed and new courses will be developed.
5- Continuing education through short upgrading courses in proposed teacher centers
will be phased in to meet annual needs.
